Subject: [Ilugc] booting with new kernel small error
In-Reply-To: <20041001062155.53185.qmail@web53708.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0410011212550.7808-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

On Thu, 30 Sep 2004, Naveen S wrote:

> -------------------------------------------------
> VFS cannot open root device "LABLE=/"
> Please append a correct "root=" boot option 
> Kernel panic VFS unable to mount fs on 00:00
> -------------------------------------------------

Boot with your orinal kernel and find out / partition

$ df -H
Filesystem             Size   Used  Avail Use% Mounted on
/dev/hda1             510MB  362MB  122MB  75% /

And replace root=/dev/hda1 and reboot with new kernel

LABLE is a typo??. In conf file, it seems to be correct.

Bye :)

Bharathi S

Deepak Sarda wrote:
> Hi everyone:
> 
> I am having some trouble mounting a samba share.
> 
> This is the line from /etc/fstab:
> 
> //samba.bii.a-star.edu.sg/deepak /mnt/sambashare smbfs
> credentials=/root/.smbpass,uid=1000,gid=100,rw 0 0
> 
> uid and gid refer to the normal user login on my machine (running on SuSE 9.1)
> 
> Directory /mnt/sambashare mounts with correct permissions, but
> everything within that directory mounts with userid set to 2177.
> 
> The result is that I can create files within /mnt/sambashare but not
> within any subdirectories. A brief listing:
> 
> deepak@ip4-138-v345:/mnt/sambashare> ls -la
> total 6815748
> drwxr-xr-x  1 deepak users  4096 2004-09-29 14:56 ./
> drwxr-xr-x  3 root   root     80 2004-09-09 17:04 ../
> -rw-------  1   2177 users   532 2004-09-27 17:25 .bash_history
> -rw-r--r--  1   2177 users    14 2004-09-02 14:27 .bash_profile
> -rw-r--r--  1   2177 users    14 2004-09-02 14:27 .bashrc
> -rwxr--r--  1   2177 users  8009 2004-09-17 10:12 commoncode.py*
> [snip]
> 
> 
> Any idea how to fix this?

In the global section check if you have given proper values for mask. My 
values are shown below.

create mask = 0770
directory mask = 0750

From deepak.sarda at gmail.com  Fri Oct  1 21:19:39 2004
From: deepak.sarda at gmail.com (Deepak Sarda)
Date: Fri Oct  1 18:49:46 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] sharing soundcard in multiple programs in linux OS
In-Reply-To: <20041001124845.52933.qmail@web50303.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20041001124845.52933.qmail@web50303.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <eaac783a041001061946ac3363@mail.gmail.com>

On Fri, 1 Oct 2004 05:48:45 -0700 (PDT), konjeti sreeram
<sreeramat2000@yahoo.com> wrote:
> Hai,
>    I am sreeram.I am currently using FEDORA CORE2.Is
> it possible
> to share sound card in multiple programs.i.e in
> windows we can here
> winamp playing mp3 songs as well as we can see vedio
> songs in windows
> media player at the same time.But i found it is not
> possibling in linux
> os.When i am using XMMS player at the same time i
> opened a vedio song
> from MplAYER.It is not playing and i senn some error
> message"your soundcard in use".please tell me how i
> can use soundcard
> in multiple programs.
You can use a software sound mixer to do this job. Which mixer u use
depends on whether you are using Gnome or KDE.

The mixer program for Gnome is called esound daemon while the one for
KDE is called arts. On of these should be running by default.

so if it's arts (u r running KDE) then u could you something like 
$ mplayer -ao arts myfile.avi 

while in XMMS, from preferences, you can choose output plugin to be arts.

Similar procedure if u r on esd (gnome) 

$mplayer -ao esd myfile.avi

and output plugin esd in xmms

-

deepak

Subject: [Ilugc] adding anther OS bootloder in grub config
In-Reply-To: <20041001124717.52292.qmail@web50303.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20041001124717.52292.qmail@web50303.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <415DD177.5060803@symonds.net>

konjeti sreeram wrote:
> I am sreeram.I am currently using FEDORA CORE2.If i
> installed 
> suse personal linux in my another partition how can i
> add that
> boot file in my LILO config.Please tell me.

Since you are running FC2, I assume that you GRUB and not LILO. I wonder 
  why you are bothere about LILO configuration file.

Anyway, if you install SuSE, tell the installer not to install the boot 
loader in MBR. Instead, write the boot loader in the BR of the partition 
you install. Assuming you install SuSE in /dev/hda2, your entry in GRUB 
configuration file (/boot/grub/menu.lst of FC2) will be

title SuSE Linux
rootnoverify (hd0,1)
chainloader +1

  Does the USB DSL modem (supplied with the unlimited plan) have a 
Linux driver? If so, all you need is a Pentium/133 with a USB interface,
16 MB RAM, a small hard drive (say 500 MB) or CDROM, and an Ethernet card
to set up a dedicated Linux router - it can be done for Rs.2500 or less,
depending on what pieces you can find for free.

  Almost all the difficulty lies in the USB modem - try to find its
model number and ask about Linux drivers from Touchtel. If the drivers
are binary-only, it's a bit of a pain, but still manageable. 

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sun Oct  3 00:10:53 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sun Oct  3 00:35:04 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Regarding cross compilation [windows and linux]
In-Reply-To: <20041002175722.8778.qmail@web54110.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041002184053.D03A2329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> How to create console graphics programs in linux?
> I need some library header file similar to conio.h in linux gcc i.e.,
> header file xxx.h that contains functions like getch() and clrscr();in gcc???

Use curses or ncurses. It's a different API, but has similar functionality.

> How to cross compile and create windows executables in linux???
> Have any body of you used such c and c++ compilers and succeeded in
> creating windows executables from linux

  It depends on the API - you can't actually create an executable that
links to MFC or similar Windows crap because that's closed. However,
if you use a closs-platform API like Mono, or Microsoft's Unix services
for Windows, you can write apps that can be compiled for either
Linux or Windows targets - but you'll have to build it on the appropriate
build host.

  You can also use Wine, VMs or emulation to run VC++ in a Windows session
under Linux.

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sun Oct  3 09:39:48 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sun Oct  3 10:03:58 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] OT: Obsolescent hardware, E-waste and salvage
In-Reply-To: <d60e5b0f04100220093d14d861@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20041003040948.E141B329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> Interesting. I thought it was difficult to buy this kind of outdated
> hardware. One can always ask around , I guess.
> 
  You can't buy anything other than P4s and Athlons new, but you can always
find scrap 486s and above easily - there were a lot of them made. Intel
sold ~100M classic Pentium CPUs, and most of them are still in the field,
being discarded or phased out slowly. Probably about 30-40% of them have
the buggy FPU, and Intel has agreed to honour the lifetime warranty by
replacing those CPUs on request - so they've got to maintain stock of
probably 10s of million Pentium classic CPU for warranty replacement.
Add it all up, there are lots of Pentium CPUs out there. There are even
more PIIs and Celerons in the field. Every single one of them can be easily
re-purposed as a router or a fileserver with a suitable Linux/*BSD reinstall.

This is one of the reasons that HP, Dell and the other server vendors
would like to remove and recycle old x86 hardware, rather than allowing
them back into the secondary market - it would cut into sales of new hardware,
which carry much higher pricetags and margins. So they offer good trade-in
deals on older hardware. Recently, they've introduced the E-waste meme to
try to pick up these systems for recycling (to them, naturally) rather than
let them get donated or resold in the secondary market (actually, they don't
mind if you toss the machine into the dumpster, they just don't want it to get
resold downstream). 

(There is a lot of E-waste generated, but PCs, especially after the early
90s, are not the major culprit. A single proprietary minicomputer like a
VAX or an AS/400 generates far more E-waste by weight and volume than even
several dozen PCs. And most of the minicomputer E-waste can't be reused,
unlike PCs. In a PC, the monitor can be reused, various parts including
the cables, drives and memories can be reused, the case can often be reused
or the steel from the case recovered, leaving only some cards and motherboard
as scrap. That's only about 5% by volume of the original system. Printers
and peripherals are another story - almost all their weight and volume
is scrap.)

-Siva

I think you are trying to upgrade PHP in a box where the Apache2 was

PHP can be upgraded  when Apache2 is installed as RPM.

> 

>I changed the swapiness to 100.  Feeling comfortable now.

100 is max swap (for RAM > 128 MB)
0 is no swap (for RAM =< 256 )
default is 60.

You can

module is loaded and load it if not (google).
Or
2. I think there should be some be some option 
wherein you can load the modules you want soon after
the install process starts.
(It is long since I used redhat. so i am sorry ; i can't remember; i
remember debian installer carrying such
an option)
Or
3. I also have a wild idea running through my mind that involves using
dd to do a bit-by-bit copy. I am not sure.

Whenever I am trying to introduce GNU/Linux to a new person, after explaining 
all the great features, the one immediate question they ask (may be to hide
their ignorance) is 

1. If it is so good, then how come everybody (they know) is using windows.
My usual answer is that GNU/Linux is catching up and already has a 
significant server marker share... blah blah blah.

'blah blah ..;' - because this fact alone seems not to be impressive
enough to the other
person in most cases. So any other (convincing) answer.

It is even more irritating when I am posting some technical article in
a group (our college)
and some stupid ass comes over and asks... if windows is so bad; how
is it the most
used os in the world then. I know that it is not by choice.

The thing is I don't want to waste my time engaging in a ramble/flame war with 
these lazy asses, who did n't care to venture beyond the
default/defunt . So if there is any authoritative article which would
nail the point...please share it.

Or should we leave it to pull. Pushing info/advocacy does n't work. Is it?

People use Linux as a symbol of their freedom of choice and so as not 
to be dependent on an Organization whose motives are driven by the
NYSE.

What others use should never be an issue with a Linux user.
Exactly why, flame wars are useless.

Your duty as a GNU/Linux user is to spread the message and let the other 
person choose. 
It's left to the individual to choose what he thinks is best.
If after all this he thinks Windows is better , so be it.

For him, Ignorance is Bliss.....

The Linux developers are(were) never in a popularity war with any other
Operating System or an Organization. They do what they feel is right
and developments on other Operating Systems hardly matter to them.

If someone feels that an interesting development has taken place and it 
would do Linux a lot of good, they go ahead and port it.

The GOAL of Linux is "To develop the Best Operating System" and not 
"Develop a better OS than Windows".

Exactly. You have brought out the mindset of a lot of users. Normally 
migration to Linux depends on various factors like the person's 
willingness to face risks/challenges, time that he can spend to learn to 
use/customize Linux, the support he gets, finding alternatives for the 
frequently used Windows tools, etc. I have come across quite a lot of 
people who advocate for Linux. According to me, two basic qualifications 
for such persons are able to attract others giving reasonable answers to 
newbies/non-adoptors queries and the next being so important that being 
patient to the response from them. No one is in a compulsion to take 
your advocacy. He may ask some questions. Some being interesting and 
some being non-sense. But they do what they should. In my experience, 
people who ask a lot of silly questions started loving Linux a lot 
compared to the people who say it's nice and forget that from there.

From vallinayagam at ureach.com  Tue Oct  5 14:48:48 2004
From: vallinayagam at ureach.com (V.K.Vallinayagam)
Date: Wed Oct  6 00:19:04 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Popularity of Windows
Message-ID: <200410051848.OAA27687@www23.ureach.com>


Hi,
 My opinion is linux can become popular only with sufficient
push from corporates. Open-source developers contribution is
insufficient. The reasons are as follows.
 We should analyse how technology is evolving. The evolution of
technology is driven by need to improve productivity.
Productivity is useful work done by an individual in per unit of
time.
  Here is the sequence in which technology evolved historically
1. Manual labor was used for most work
   Industrialisation brought steam power and it replaced manual
labor.Later came electrical power to replace steam and heavily
replaced manual labor. Eg. Water pump draws water from well.
2. The decision making aspect and computational aspects were
done manually. Then came electronics and control systems that
relieved man of programmable decisions.Eg. U need not remember
to switch off motor for water pump.
3. In this phase, people had to write programs to make these
control systems act intelligently.Then came the quest to reduce
the lines of programs written.
   In this phase many approaches like object-oriented,
open-source came so that reuse could be high.
4. In the next phase, number of lines were reduced but people
were forced to know a lot about libraries and components to get
that re-use. Though the coding is reduced, knowing became more.
  In this phase, the quest came to find ways to get things with
minimum knowledge.
 
  Here came gui and others.

 Therefore future world, people's productivity is dependent on
getting more things done with knowing less. To be precise,
information-hiding. 
  End-users want information-hiding, open source developers are
against it. For example, Eric Raymond, in his book on hackers
culture and unix elaborates why hackers are not comfortable with
Object-Oriented approach.
  In essence windows does information-hiding from end-users
point but hackers work, OS or any other software generally does
not,but technically hacker's work is superior.
  Therefore some corporate entity needs to package hacker's work
and give it in a way that hides unnecessary information for
end-user.
  This we call as "user-friendliness"

Regards
V.K.Vallinayagam

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Wed Oct  6 06:55:12 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Wed Oct  6 07:21:20 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Popularity of Windows
In-Reply-To: <200410051848.OAA27687@www23.ureach.com>
Message-ID: <20041006012512.186F7329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
>  My opinion is linux can become popular only with sufficient
> push from corporates. Open-source developers contribution is
> insufficient. The reasons are as follows.

  You may not be aware of the recent statistics from Andrew
Morton that show that over 95% of the patches to the kernel
now come from Open-source developers who are employed specifically
for that purpose by large corporates like IBM, Intel, HP, etc.
In other words, Linux is already being corporatized, like it or not.
Various other userland pieces also have similar corporate backing,
like gcc (RedHat), netfilter/iptables (Watchguard), and so on.

  Your notion that open-source volunteers are unpaid volunteers,
hackers, hobbyists or students in Universities was true in the
early stages of the GNU/Linux movement, but is no longer that
cut and dried.

>   End-users want information-hiding, open source developers are
> against it. For example, Eric Raymond, in his book on hackers
> culture and unix elaborates why hackers are not comfortable with
> Object-Oriented approach.

  Again too simplistic - Some end-users want information hiding,
some what transparency. In particular, sysadmins and IT departments
generally prefer the latter, since it simplifies backup, migration
and general system maintenance.

  The notion that hackers are uncomfortable with OO methodology is
simplistic - this entire ecosystem of a billion+ lines of code could
not have been written without a structure. Whether you want
to call it OO or structured programming or modularity or whatever 
IT buzzword is currently in vogue is upto you, but most open source
users and developers don't care. All that matters is that the code
is correct; easy to read, maintain and extend; and interoperates
well (all of this applies to good FLOSS code, but rarely to
proprietary code).

-Siva 
From vinothv at gmail.com  Tue Oct  5 22:05:14 2004
From: vinothv at gmail.com (Vinoth Kumar)
Date: Wed Oct  6 07:35:22 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Popularity of Windows
In-Reply-To: <20041006003801.92A0D1DB258@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <3779a1e704100503406cb1e455@mail.gmail.com>
	<20041006003801.92A0D1DB258@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <ccbd9cbf041005190547b55c2e@mail.gmail.com>

Its not about Open source contributors buddies. The magic of windows
lies in the OEM (Original Equipment Manufaturer). The smart guy
manages to make every product manufacturer make drivers for windows,
while they pay money to keep the 'Strategical Partnership' with
Microsoft. Apparently, its coz windows makes their product sell
better. And in most cases its true. Most ppl use windows, so if they
make driver for it its gonna sell better. When I buy something new
from the market, I am not sure if  I may be able to use it with my
Linux, but I can be certain that it will work under windows.

The problem is the license. Most of them dont want to give away the
source code (they have every right to do so). Many have the wrong
impression that drivers got to be open source too. With LGPL and so
many variants of GPL, it is possible to release just the compiled
binaries. They could release binaries for just few popular distros,
and others can request for binary from their website. This kinda
concept needs to be given a push, but unfortunately the hard-core open
source enthusists wouldn't like it that way.

Good news is that, some manufaturers have started releasing drivers
for linux with their products. Esp in server side, its very common now
to get a SCSI adpater with rpm or deb package with it.

If more and more ppl start using Linux (which is the eventuality), the
manufacturers will be forced to give drivers that in turn makes linux
more popular. There cud be nothing stopping the linux at that time.
Open source is the way to go for a healthier, honest future.

At this point, however, the debate that which operating system is
better for desktop is still debatable.

One last point: Linux simply rocks!  


--
cheers
Vinoth

                                    -- One fuckin smart guy

Yes you can access any device connected to serial/parallel port using C
functions like open,read,write, close etc... which is treated as file.

Read the man page of "open" function.

All you need to know is the protocol messages for your device.

From raamanp at yahoo.co.in  Wed Oct  6 05:49:30 2004

Whole of free software isn't as popular as proprietory software,
because lack of advertising,marketing... and all other business
methods.

In view of lack of business potential[to make tons of money], the
only way Free software can be popularised is by personal contacts. In
the early days, the net wasn't as developed as it is now,
constraining development and tranmission. With improvement in net we
see Free software gaining popluarity. 

Rather than looking at popularity of two OSes we should think in
terms of clash of idealogy of Free/Opensource vs. Proprietory.

In the last two years of my talks at various colleges,corporates
etc.,
I think people apreciate principles to which Free/opensource stands
for than simple popularity.

Let's not bother how popular Linux is, let's bother about its
purpose.

Raman.P

From vsst at ipr.res.in  Wed Oct  6 11:00:36 2004

Subject: [Ilugc] Serial Device Programming
In-Reply-To: <20041006044944.85A921DB290@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.GSO.4.10.10410061053160.1490-100000@sun4.plasma.ernet.in>


Hello,
       Go through the serial device programming for POSIX operating system
guide located at http://www.easysw.com/~mike/serial/serial.html.


     /dev/ttyS0 or /dev/ttyS1 is your serial device (equivalent to COM1
and COM2 in windows).
        First you have to set baudrate,stop bit, number of bits,parity all
those things in your program(the guide above says how to do it) as per the
specifications given in the manual of the product.
   you can use read and write syscalls to send data and read data from the
device.

Similar to hyperterminal, you have an app called cutecom in linux. First
you check
whether the device is responding to your protocols(#XX command) i.e you
get any reply from the device in response to this command.

From g.bharath at gmail.com  Wed Oct  6 12:56:24 2004
From: g.bharath at gmail.com (Bharath.G)
Date: Wed Oct  6 12:56:37 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Serial device programming
In-Reply-To: <20041006063002.2A55C1DB25F@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20041006063002.2A55C1DB25F@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <4937d2e8041006002662331c1f@mail.gmail.com>

Hey Varun,

               Well the serial devices in Linux would be /dev/ttySX or
USB serial /dev/usb/ttyUSBX, /dev/ttyUSBX.
 
To read / write from a serial device, open the serial device as a file
handle/descriptor, you could set permissions whilist the "open" 
call.There are different modes of reading from the serial port -
Canonical,non cannonical and the asychronous mode(Signalling). Writing
would be relatively easy,but reading from the serial port can be a
little shitty unless you really know what you want to do, you will get
stuck whilist reading characters in Raw mode. The Termios is used for
setting the serial port parameters.

Take a look at this guide for programming in different modes,

http://www.faqs.org/docs/Linux-HOWTO/Serial-Programming-HOWTO.html ..

use minicom (teminal) or Tip or even write a small terminal code for
debugging thro serial ports,

Alternatively u can use this code for a start , 

//Author-G.Bharath
//Co-ordinates - g.bharath@gmail.com

#define COMPORT "/dev/usb/ttyUSB3"  //SET PORT PATHNAME HERE
#define MAX_CHAR 1 //No of chars to be transmitted

//File Handle

int fd; //file descriptor 
char recvd_char[2];
//Terminal settings

struct termios tiop;

int Init_Com_Port(void)
{

	fd = open(COMPORT,O_RDWR | O_NOCTTY | O_NONBLOCK);
	
	if(tcgetattr(fd,&tiop)<0)
   	{
       		printf("Error getting terminal settings ERRNO %d \n",errno);
		return(-1);
       		//exit(0);
//Alternatively get and store attributes to a differnt termios
structure so that
// you can restore the old settings when u app quits!

   	}
   
           //terminal settings
	
	//Set Baud Rate to 19200
	cfsetispeed(&tiop,B19200); //Set printer port speed to 9600
	cfsetospeed(&tiop,B19200); // input and output
	
	// set No parity 8N1
	tiop.c_cflag |= (CLOCAL | CREAD);
	tiop.c_cflag &= ~PARENB;
	tiop.c_cflag &= ~CSTOPB;
	tiop.c_cflag |= CS8;

	//Disable Hardware Flow Control
	
	//tio.c_cflag &= ~CNEW_CRTSCTS; 
	
	//Raw Input mode
	
	tiop.c_lflag &= ~(ICANON | ECHO |ECHOE | ISIG); 
	
	//deselect cannonical ,echo and signal modes
	
	//Disable Software Flow Control
	
	tiop.c_iflag &= ~(IXON | IXOFF | IXANY);

	//Raw output mode
	
	tiop.c_oflag &= ~OPOST;

	//tiop.c_cc[VMIN]  = 0;
	//tiop.c_cc[VTIME] = 1;
   
	if(tcsetattr(fd,TCSANOW,&tiop)<0)
   	{
   		printf("Error in storing terminal settings ERRNO %d\n",errno);
		return(-1);
	}

	
	return(1);
}

void transmit_char(char *ptr)
{
	write(fd,ptr,MAX_CHAR);
}

void get_char(void)
{
	unsigned char byte_recvd;

	do
	{
	   byte_recvd=read(fd,recvd_char,1); //Read until one char is read
	}while(byte_recvd<=0); 

//copy recvd_char[0] to your mem buffer .....
//Make sure u give a char pointer to the read call it expects it
}

to use signals use the code in the tutorial,if u really want
Asychronous data transfer,

Regards

Bharath.G
Embeded Software Dude 
Chennai.

From arvy at kongu.ac.in  Wed Oct  6 18:19:04 2004
From: arvy at kongu.ac.in (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Wed Oct  6 18:28:00 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] postgresql installation
In-Reply-To: <20041006114513.92236.qmail@web41115.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20041006114513.92236.qmail@web41115.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <1097066944.6379.17.camel@slice.kongu.edu>

Installing postgresql will require some experience in basic linux
administration. Judging by your email, I personally feel it would be
better if you asked one of your friends to help you out. Or you can use
a postgresql over the network if you are in a networked environment and
if it is available on one of the machines in the network.

And by the way, it is `rpm-qa | grep stuff` and not "\" as you had
specified; about the 'where to type' question, you need to type this in
any place where you can see a shell prompt. Possible places in a GUI
environment are Konsole, xterm, kterm, gterm, rxvt, et al.



Regards,
Arvind Kalyan

On Thu, 07 Oct 2004 11:41:42 +0530, Arvind Kalyan <arvy@kongu.ac.in> wrote:
> Google for htpasswd
 
http://httpd.apache.org/docs-2.0/howto/auth.html


Here's the basics of password protecting a directory on your server.

You'll need to create a password file. This file should be placed
somewhere not accessible from the web. This is so that folks cannot
download the password file. For example, if your documents are served
out of /usr/local/apache/htdocs you might want to put the password
file(s) in /usr/local/apache/passwd.

To create the file, use the htpasswd utility that came with Apache.
This will be located in the bin directory of wherever you installed
Apache. To create the file, type:

htpasswd -c /usr/local/apache/passwd/passwords rbowen 

htpasswd will ask you for the password, and then ask you to type it
again to confirm it:

# htpasswd -c /usr/local/apache/passwd/passwords rbowen
New password: mypassword
Re-type new password: mypassword
Adding password for user rbowen 

If htpasswd is not in your path, of course you'll have to type the
full path to the file to get it to run. On my server, it's located at
/usr/local/apache/bin/htpasswd

Next, you'll need to configure the server to request a password and
tell the server which users are allowed access. You can do this either
by editing the httpd.conf file or using an .htaccess file. For
example, if you wish to protect the directory
/usr/local/apache/htdocs/secret, you can use the following directives,
either placed in the file /usr/local/apache/htdocs/secret/.htaccess,
or placed in httpd.conf inside a <Directory
/usr/local/apache/apache/htdocs/secret> section.

AuthType Basic
AuthName "Restricted Files"
AuthUserFile /usr/local/apache/passwd/passwords
Require user rbowen 



-- 
Thanks and regards
Tom

Dhanagopal Rengasamy wrote:
 > I don't know
 >whether the mandrkae has
 >inbuilt postgresql ...

try:
# which postgres

if the response is:
# /usr/bin/postgres
postgres is installed and in the same directory, you would find psql,
createdb, createuser etc.

If postgres was installed from an rpm package, try:
#  rpm -q postgres

postgres-7.0.2-29 or something like that would be displayed if postgres
is installed. Otherwise, you may have to do an installation.

You may also try browsing through the installed deb and rpm packages
using a gui tool like kpackage. HTH.



From lug at chandrashekar.info  Thu Oct  7 19:33:39 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Thu Oct  7 19:34:06 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Check the support of xpm,png..
In-Reply-To: <20041007094448.91503.qmail@web51703.mail.yahoo.com>
References: <20041007093912.GA30862@symonds.net>
	<20041007094448.91503.qmail@web51703.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20041007193339.6af13c7f.lug@chandrashekar.info>

> If the packages are installed using 'tar', then how do
> I find?

If you've done source install (untar, ./configure ; make ; make
install), you should try using 'checkinstall' instead of the 'make
install' command. This works on Slackware, dont know about RedHat and
its derivatives. It updates your package repositories so that you can
uninstall or get your package listed using package-specific commands.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From boose at eth.net  Fri Oct  8 21:09:18 2004
From: boose at eth.net (boovarahan s)
Date: Fri Oct  8 21:23:47 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Popularity of windows
Message-ID: <4166B4A6.5050709@eth.net>

May I request M/s Praveen & Mohanraj  to be soft in their expression ?

I am a middle aged man working as a Clerk in Canara Bank. And we are 
using DOS based softwares in our Bank. Slowly we are having Windows OS 
(Windows 2000). Although there is no necessity for me to have a PC in my 
home, I purchased one in 2000 and the assembler installed Windows OS. 
Neither me nor the vendor had any idea of  Linux or Open Source 
Software  at that time. Last year I heard about Linux  in newspapers. 
Accidentally I subscribed for LFY. It is thro LFY only I came to know of 
linux and its power. In the meanwhile my hard disk had to be formatted 
quite a number of times following virus attack in spite of having an 
anti virus program duly updated at regular intervals. Frustrated with 
this I decided to give linux a try.
Without any formal study of computers/software , I tried to install 
Redhat on my own. With quite a bit of  struggling, I successfully had it 
for a week.
Then Thro ilugc I chanced upon meeting Mr Balachander from Adyar who 
gave me Mandrake 9.2 CDs  and it was just a cakewalk to install MDK 9.2. 
Thro ilugc I contacted Mr Sridhar who gave me MDK 10 which presently I'm 
using.

I'd like to put before you all the following points:
1. A good number of computer users are non techies / amateurs who are 
guided by the assemblers / vendors who use mostly pirated Windows OS. We 
should find a way to promote news about Linux to these group of people.

2. Most  of these people including the assemblers won't waste their 
brain by using it by undergoing the tedius task of  insatlling linux. 
Instead they would prefer to insert the OS CD, run the setup program, 
give the serial number and relax.

3.Most of the elders and middle aged people buy computers as a status 
symbol and they don't use it at all and their wards are not mature 
enough to know of Open Source Software. It is the college students , 
that too in the engineering colleges, evince interest in linux. In most 
of  the offices, people do not know at all about linux. In my nephew's 
school in Tambaram (which is quite big and famous), the computer teacher 
does not know anything of linux. In a garment factory where I had gone 
to canvass, they were using Windows OS only and nobody was there who had 
ever heard of the word linux.

4. Even for those who venture out to install linux, there is proper 
guidance. Even after continuously using linux for the past 9 months, 
still I do not know the commands since I'm using it in the GUI mode 
only. The use of books is of little help as things are different in the 
books and in the PC.

It is my notion that most of the ilugc members are engineering students 
or software professionals and amateurs like are a minority. It would be 
nice, if somebody devouts a little bit of his/her time to conduct a 
class during week ends to help people like me to learn linux.

I hope some day somebody will come to my rescue .

Until then good bye.

Boovarahan S

this is a series of excellent points on why several people who are not 
techies / geeks / kernel hackers etc decide to make a shift to linux 
from windows.

just one point to add to his email:

as a matter of fact even the people who bundle linux preinstalled (acer, 
hp etc)

1. install an outdated version of linux like rh9

2. leave lots of space free on the disk - their install is at the most a 
base install of a few hundred mb .. 1 gb and the rest of the disk is 
unpartitioned.  they think selling a box with rh9 or maybe even pc-dos 
means they dont have to worry about MS chasing them with license audits, 
and most people buying it are buying it as a cheap system and will just 
install pirated windows 2k / xp on it later.

the rh install on the acer travelmate had several key drivers like 
centrino wireless etc not working] .. installing slak 10 and downloading 
/ configuring stuff, recompiling kernels for several days on end was fun.

so - you also need people to ship viable OEM installs of linux before it 
really becomes popular.

That's a good point. Before 6 months we purchased one system from a vendor.
I installed redhat 9 and the NIC has not working. You know what the vendor
told. He said the NIC was working when he tested it with windows and linux
has damanged the NIC. Panic!. I again asked him to demonstrate how NIC
worked in Windows. So installed win98(?) and it showed the NIC card. He
thought simply showing the device in the list is working. But it never
worked(when try to ping). Only then he accepted to change the NIC. So we
should have plans, before we teach them(vendors).
> 2. Most  of these people including the assemblers won't waste their

> give the serial number and relax.

abc, reboot, reboot???(This is only for Win98, which is still the most
popular OS among home users AFAIK).But in linux you can install all apps in
a single stroke. That's one more advantage i see. 

I have seen people who convert the linux desktop to resemble windows look &
feel. I think, they never want to change. If they like one they stick to it
and be happy with it whether it satisfies their needs or not(this is my own
opinion and please correct me if i am wrong).

> 4. Even for those who venture out to install linux, there is proper
> guidance. Even after continuously using linux for the past 9 months,
> still I do not know the commands since I'm using it in the GUI mode
> only. The use of books is of little help as things are different in the

my experience. i our office i recommended Linux and all systems have only
Linux(except 5 dualbooted with windows xp). When new people come they dont
find it difficult. I just show them the browser, the directory to store the
files, and the applications to work. They dont know the commands(and i
think they dont have to). It just works fine. After 9 months of work all
the users are happy. This is from my exp.

When common people use windows. If there is problem they call the vendor and
fix it. Using linux, they have no help, so have to do their own. I think
educating the vendors and assemblers will help lot in spreading linux to
common people. So that when home users come accross problems they can get
come help(for which they will be charged).

From ramanraj at md4.vsnl.net.in  Sun Oct 10 09:56:29 2004
From: ramanraj at md4.vsnl.net.in (Ramanraj K)
Date: Sun Oct 10 09:45:12 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] .^. Calpp Project
References: <20040930151113.DED8F329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
Message-ID: <4168B9F5.4010404@md4.vsnl.net.in>

Hi Bharathi & Sivasankar.  I was a little disappointed that you missed 
the talk on Calpp, because it would have been nice to have convinced you 
to contribute to the Calpp Project.  But, I would like to thank all of 
you for having given the opportunity, because many offered support to 
the Calpp Project, immediately after the talk :)

Before me, Hari talked about Zhakanini, the Tamil PC Project and the 
work done by Writer Sujatha, Siva and the other team members.  Kumar 
revealed that Debian has included the Tamil support from its web site 
last week.   Hari explained about using KBabel and other tools that are 
used to create the .po files that handle translation.  It seems about 
one lakh lines have been translated so far. Hari also shared his notes 
on the Indic Font meet that he attended at Mumbai.

When I started the talk on Calpp, I could not resist mentioning about 
the greatest contribution to legal jurisprudence, which is Avvayar's 
Athichoodi - the Tamil Needhi Nool.  It is well impossible to simplify 
the law any better: High ethics and morals can be taught to primary 
school children in the formative years itself. Avvayar's elegant and 
succulent Tamil maxims would beat its Latin brocard cousins hands down. 
"man parittu unnel" [gist of property law], "giam pada urai", "kandu 
onru sollel" [law of evidence], "ooram sollel" [be fair], "por thozhil 
puriyel" - "don't do the business of war" [the very essence of 
international law] are all worth heeding. Now, that forced me to start 
with an apology for Calpp:  we need to use computers to get back to 
those innocent times ;)

I started the talk with what a typical legal application might look 
like.  The legal procedures in about 90% of the total, are mostly well 
defined and structured, with the little balance lying in the grey area 
of doubt and philosophy. A major bulk of the law could be easily 
computerised with free software and good research.  I briefly explained 
Section 4 of the TN Buildings (Lease and Rent Control) Act, 1960 with 
reference to the javascript application at 
http://personal.vsnl.com/ramanraj/kr_tnfrc.html This is an example of a 
typical self-documenting legal application, and one can get a good feel 
of what coding the law would be like.  It includes data validation, data 
conversion, test cases, generation of reasons for the computation, along 
with all documentation required to manually check the result. Calpp 
could manage hundreds of such legal applications, and it could maintain 
the legal system with minimum effort.

I did not mention one of my itches for the Calpp Project: Several years 
ago, when a five year old school boy was walking back home, a reckless 
public bus driver hit him from behind, and as a result of the injuries 
sustained in the accident, the boy became a paraplegic, losing vital 
body functions below the waist.  He claimed 100k, as compensation, but 
was granted only about 25k.  In the appeal, it was doubled to ~50K. This 
was inspite of rulings that paraplegia is a condition worse than death, 
and had awarded upto 1200k as compensation. The unfortunate boy got his 
50k after several years of litigation and, after all that, the boy's 
guardians merely said, the boy is cheerful about his fate, doing well in 
his studies, and that he will stand on his own feet [ironically, the boy 
may never be able to do that literally]. The pyrrhic victory of 
"doubling" the compensation is of no solace, and even though many 
willingly accept life as it comes, it would be a shame if we did not use 
whatever we know and are capable of, to improve the situation around us.

Computers could efficiently speed up proceedings and help in rendering 
substantial justice to people in need.

More generally, law is common for all, and reducing the legal system to 
machine executable free code would benefit all.

Edsger W.Dijkstra said:

<quote>
For me, the first challenge for computing science is to discover how to
maintain order in a finite, but very large, discrete universe that is
intricately intertwined. And a second, but not less important challenge
is how to mould what you have achieved in solving the first problem,
into a teachable discipline: it does not suffice to hone your own
intellect (that will join you in your grave), you must teach others how
to hone theirs. The more you concentrate on these two challenges, the
clearer you will see that they are only two sides of the same coin:
teaching yourself is discovering what is teachable.
</quote source: EWD 709: My hopes of computing science>

After reading EW Dijkstra, I realised that, the Calpp project,
predominantly meant for "legal" procedures and proceedings, could be on
the path to discovery in the direction of the first challenge of CS.

Law is about maintaining order and peace in this discrete universe.  The
Calpp goal has been to find the easiest and shortest way to store and
run legal procedures and proceedings, wherefrom we could measure the
extent of peace and order in this universe, and hopefully control them.

Calpp is at present runnable, testable and one could play a lot with it
and use it as well to both write new procedures and run them as
proceedings.  For well defined procedures, it can generate the required 
forms, do data validation, data conversion, storage, report generation, 
and handle workflow with minimum effort. It has a good indexing system, 
that may not get simpler than what it is.

Calpp could look more neat, have more features, and have every useful 
procedure added to it.

While most legal procedures would require considerable legal research, 
sys procedures need expertise in computing. Many sys admin tasks could 
also be included as procedures.  During the talk, I suggested including 
procedures for writing the apache conf file,etc.  Unless one understands 
the logic behind the conf, it is almost impossible to write a useful 
procedure.

Please let me know if you would be interested in the Calpp Project.
http://gborg.postgresql.org/project/calpp/projdisplay.php

Your participation could help and make a big difference :)

Regards,
Ramanraj.

 >
 > let me give my requirements in layman's words
 >
 > the application can have the following features
 >
 > 1) based on number of  "pullis" [dots ], it should generate KOLAM ...


You could develop a kolam extension for GIMP using Script-Fu
http://www.gimp.org

Writing to the gimp dev team, showing them a few kolams, and the steps 
involved in drawing kolams may yield good clues, and you may even have 
your done by someone who is an expert in Script-Fu.  Gimp supports Perl 
scripts also.

To get started on this, open Gimp, and under the Xtns menu, select 
Script-Fu > Console ... There is a DB Browser that displays several 
built in functions that could draw dots, lines and curves, change 
colors, introduce animation etc.  Good luck  :)

Subject: We need more mailing lists (was Re: [Ilugc]
	Popularity	ofwindows)
Message-ID: <200410110629.CAA02895@www20.ureach.com>

Hi,
 I agree that one purpose of the list is to help others. But
levels of expertise matters too. One can help some thro
discussion group, if they are at a delta level below and also if
one feels that anwer to the question cannot be found in other
sources.
 If everyone spends his time educating another person thro
personal means like classroom or e-mail, it cannot be
productive. Books, electronic texts  are impersonal ways and far
more productive ways. Say one person spends 10 hours writing a
doc and 1000 people can read and get benefiited.
 There are enough FAQs, documents and other sources for newbies
in internet to educate themselves in linux.
  Moreover FAQ are older technologies. Wikis are more better.
  For reference, consult www.tldp.org, www.linuxquestions.org.
 www.linuxquestions.org has a wiki. For experts, here is my
suggestion. If someone asks a question, don't answer it. Just
show them a link in www.linuxquestions.org's wiki. If there is
no link in it, create a topic in that wiki and give its
reference.
 This way, many more people can be benefitted and it is more
productive.

Regards
V.K.Vallinayagam

> Now i am able to boot to win. However, i am unsuccessful at my
> attempts to boot linux.

Can you show us the _uncommented_ entries of /etc/lilo.conf ?

Check if you have an entry for XP as follows:

other=/dev/hda1
   Label=XP

Assuming that you wish to install Lilo on the MBR, make sure that you
also have the following entry in your lilo.conf file: 

boot=/dev/hda

Rerun /sbin/lilo once you've updated these entries.

Chandrashekar Babu.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Oct 11 18:03:18 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Oct 11 18:28:12 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Debian GNU/Hurd CDs
In-Reply-To: <416A7640.7010502@symonds.net>
Message-ID: <20041011123318.2C0FF329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> Hurd is not the kernel. Hurd is the set of servers that run on the
> GNU Mach microkernel.
> 
  This is another thing about the GNU project that's bound to irritate
a lot of people - Mach was originally developed by CMU and made available
under a CMU license that was BSD-like, and in fact required both a Unix
source license (from AT&T) and a 4.3BSD license (from Univ. of Cal.) as
pre-requisites. This applied to Mach 3.0 and earlier, and GNU contributed
absolutely *nothing* to this project while the work as done in CMU until
1994.

  Subsequently, the Univ. of Utah forked the code and continued development,
producing Mach 4.0, which has a GNU-style build environment, but again,
AFAIK, GNU contributions to the kernel codebase was still *nil*, and the
license remained the combination of AT&T, BSD and CMU, with additions.

  GNU then forked the Mach 4 codebase to produce the microkernel that is
now used in the Hurd project. There are some in-kernel device drivers
ported over from Linux, considerable documentation and a GNU-style build.
This is what goes by the name of GNU Mach, but the core microkernel remains
CMU-licensed, in addition to the other licenses, including the GPL, for the
GNU additions.

  By calling it GNU Mach, there is an insidious implication that the GPL
applies to the entire codebase. This is not true at all, and portions of
it may still belong to AT&T - this was never decided in the AT&T vs. Berkeley
consent decree that permitted free distribution of 4.4BSD (remember, only
4.4BSD-lite is legally unencumbered, not 4.3BSD).

  GNU's contribution to Mach is minimal - the fork of the Mach 4 codebase
is legally on very thin ice. There's no way that it can be safely released
under the GPL. The only way that GNU can resolve this issue is to drop Mach
altogether and go with another microkernel, like L4 or similar, which is
completely covered by the GPL. 

  Under the circumstances, even the act of naming the fork as GNU Mach is
legally shaky and should be considered unsustainable. 

-Siva

P.S. I'm not attacking the GNU project, which has brought us great code 
including gcc and glibc without which we'd be nowhere, but only the
nomenclature for this particular project to which GNU contributions are
relatively small.

Sivasankar Chander wrote:
   >>Hurd is not the kernel. Hurd is the set of servers that run on the
   >>GNU Mach microkernel.
   >>
   >
   >   GNU's contribution to Mach is minimal - the fork of the Mach 4
codebase
   > is legally on very thin ice. There's no way that it can be safely
released
   > under the GPL. The only way that GNU can resolve this issue is to
drop Mach
   > altogether and go with another microkernel, like L4 or similar, 
which is
   > completely covered by the GPL.
   >
   >   Under the circumstances, even the act of naming the fork as GNU
Mach is
   > legally shaky and should be considered unsustainable.

If an existing non-Gnu project gets dubbed as GNU software and part of
the GNU Project, it means that the project receives support from  the
GNU Project Developers, adheres to the GNU coding standard, and it
certainly  would not mean that it was built from scratch by GNU Project.

Mach appears to have a very long history, and Utah University was the
last to maintain the Mach and the oskit fork.

http://www.gnu.org/software/hurd/gnumach-doc/mach_1.html#SEC3 says:
"On May 27 2002, after the Gnumach 1.3 release, Roland McGrath merged
OSKit-Mach onto the HEAD of CVS making it the Gnumach 2.x mainline."

That settles the licensing issues, if there were any at all.

http://www.gnu.org/software/hurd/history.html
http://www.cs.utah.edu/flux/mach4/html/Mach4-proj.html
ftp://flux.cs.utah.edu/flux/oskit//README

Of course, these are my own views based on public information available
on the web.

From shuvebh at naturesoft.net  Wed Oct 13 09:11:46 2004
From: shuvebh at naturesoft.net (Shuveb Hussain)
Date: Wed Oct 13 09:17:34 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] *nix & memory cleanup
In-Reply-To: <1097587610.416bdb9a298b1@SifyCorp.com>
References: <1097587610.416bdb9a298b1@SifyCorp.com>
Message-ID: <1097673106.2384.20.camel@shuveb>

On Tue, 2004-10-12 at 09:56, ananth_g@sifycorp.com wrote:
> hi all, 
>    I have writen a C code which uses malloc(3) to allocate memory. The program is meant for running in background and is kind of a daemon. the program gets terminated by bringing to the foreground(this happens when it is attached to some terminal or when run in foreground) or by using kill. My concern is will all the memory allocated for it be cleared( it should rite?). if it gets cleared , then is there any function that i can use for using up memory even after the program is killed ( using kill), some function in C that allocates memory and which should be explicitly cleared?.
> 

Hi Ananth,

All memory allocated by a program will be reclaimed by the system when
the program exits. But it is a good practice to manage memory well
within your program, freeing it with free() when the chunk of memory in
question is no longer needed. When you tell me its a daemon, I
understand it might be running 24/7. In that case, proper memory
management in the program becomes top priority, to avoid memory leaks.
It is also important to understand that on calling free() the memory is
not immediately returned to the system. The glibc functions do internal
buffering of the memory management functions....


---
Regards,
Shuveb Hussain 
Visit my Blog www.livejournal.com/users/shuveb

Scripting

"Python-fu" is now the standard external scripting interface for Gimp

...The biggest drawback, for Gimp 2.0, is that the standard user
interface offered in Python-fu does not use the complete power of the
Python language. The interface is currently designed to support simple
scripts, but a more sophisticated version is a goal of future
development.....

....Gimp-Perl is no longer distributed with the standard Gimp 2
distribution, but is available as a separate package.

From mssnlayam at vsnl.net  Wed Oct 13 01:23:42 2004
From: mssnlayam at vsnl.net (Suriya Narayanan M S)
Date: Wed Oct 13 11:53:56 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: automating partitioning and formatting on linux
Message-ID: <20041013062342.GA27444@cs.utexas.edu>

>From the fdisk manpage (search for interactive).

There  are  several  *fdisk programs around.  Each has its
problems and strengths.  Try them  in  the  order  cfdisk,
fdisk,  sfdisk.   (Indeed,  cfdisk  is a beautiful program
that has strict requirements on the  partition  tables  it
accepts,  and  produces high quality partition tables. Use
it if you can.  fdisk is a buggy program that  does  fuzzy
things - usually it happens to produce reasonable results.
Its single advantage is that it has some support  for  BSD
disk  labels and other non-DOS partition tables.  Avoid it
if you can.  sfdisk is for hackers only - the user  inter
face  is  terrible,  but it is more correct than fdisk and
more powerful than both fdisk and  cfdisk.   Moreover,  it
can be used noninteractively.)

The short answer -- use sfdisk.

Suriya

PS: I deleted the original message. The header of this message
does not contain references to the original. Apologies.

Hi Karrupuswamy,

               If you have the 2.4.18bf4 source with you, you can
compile the driver without compiling the whole kernel. Just put this
driver in the /kernel-2.4.X/drivers/usb (or any folder), add a #define
MODULE to the driver source file (if it is not there), since you are
trying to compile for a 2.4, for 2.6 you do away with the MODULE
Macro.

make the driver from the /kernel-2.4.X folder

by make drivers/usb/usb-modem.c (just an example)

This should create a the module, insmod it should not create
problems.Put this in your /lib/modules if you need to modprobe it.Also
you can check for the module details using " modinfo ".

( Alternatively you can complie in the kernel tree, by modifying the
makefile, guess you wanted to do away with that)

Regards

Bharath.G

From arvy at kongu.ac.in  Wed Oct 13 13:13:41 2004
From: arvy at kongu.ac.in (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Wed Oct 13 13:14:17 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] defragment linux
In-Reply-To: <416BE3E4.2080806@frodo.hserus.net>
References: <20041012135242.81096.qmail@web53701.mail.yahoo.com>
	<416BE3E4.2080806@frodo.hserus.net>
Message-ID: <1097653421.6380.13.camel@slice.kongu.edu>

Linux/unix systems dont need 'defrag'. Its the way files are referenced
(using inodes, and inode tables) that aid nix systems in getting over
the 'split up data' and 'wheres the next free block?' syndrome.

fsck merely checks and repairs broken fs, doesn't relocate data like
defrag does. And yes, there *is* a 'defrag' utility, for linux, which
you can get from googling around. But it is not necessary.

regards,
Arvind Kalyan

> ext3 and other journaling systems wont need defragging to the extent

From arvy at kongu.ac.in  Wed Oct 13 13:22:26 2004

Date: Wed Oct 13 13:22:55 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] automating partitioning and formatting on linux
In-Reply-To: <20041013060941.6FA112B2B86@ws5-7.us4.outblaze.com>
References: <20041013060941.6FA112B2B86@ws5-7.us4.outblaze.com>
Message-ID: <1097653946.6362.18.camel@slice.kongu.edu>

If all the /dev/hdb that you are going to connect are going to be of
same size, then just `dd` the MBR of one preformatted disk and restore
the dd content to a new /dev/hdb each time the script is executed. You
can ofcourse run mkfs to 'format' the partition.

regards,
arv

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Thu Oct 14 02:21:03 2004
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Thu Oct 14 02:11:28 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Sshd - unusual mode
In-Reply-To: <20041013060849.34ACB1DB25C@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
References: <20041013060849.34ACB1DB25C@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <20041013205103.GC10630@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

S Mohan wrote:
> I've to provide access to an application using ssh. The application has
> authorisation built in. I do not want the user to give two passwords. In
> fact, I do not want users to have system accounts at all.

> I tried sshd with PermitRootLogin without-password and this did not work. I
> know the hazards of a open root login. The program will be the user's shell
> in /etc/passwd thus denying him a shell.

Here is how you do this -

WARNING:
  This system is tested only with ssh and is untested with rsh.  I recommend
  that you entirely disable rsh on the machine that runs this.  In the worst
  case, someone can run arbitrary programs as user foo using rsh.  Definitely
  not something you want!!

1. Create a new user account with "adduser foo".
2. Set user foo's shell to your application.
3. Delete user foo's password with "passwd -d foo"
4. Ensure you have "nullok" in /etc/pam.d/common-password, otherwise users
   with blank passwords cannot login.  Note: introduces a potential security
   risk.

5. Create a ssh key pair for user foo eg. run "ssh-keygen -t dsa"
6. Copy ~foo/.ssh/id_dsa.pub ~foo/.ssh/authorized_keys
7. The authorized_keys file should contain a single line.  Add the following
   to the start of the line -
    no-port-forwarding,no-X11-forwarding,no-agent-forwarding

When you run "ssh foo@hostname", your application will start immediately.
This should also work with putty, et al.

Note:
  This system is very secure and cannot be circumvented by running
  "ssh foo@hostname /bin/sh", etc.  In this case, the "/bin/sh" will be passed
  as a command line argument to your application.  Invoke your app through a
  simple shell script wrapper if this bothers you.


Using a similar approach, I run secure anon CVS without using the cvs pserver.

HTH,

- Raja

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Thu Oct 14 10:19:50 2004

Hi ignacius,

We have good progress about it. I am confident that soon we will have
solution (if anybody is successful with this modem type, as i have
mentioned below, it is nice to inform through this mailing list). Here
is the history.

I too have touchtel 64kbps ADSL modem. I have started installing it on
Debian 3.0.r2.
My modem is Conexant ADSL Modem of vendor id: 0x0572 and product id:
0xcb06 (You have to check yours from any Windows installation done by
Touchtel). I have two options of driver.
1. accessrunner driver
2. olitec Aethra StarModem driver

Now I am working on olitec driver.:
1.I have installed kernel source 2.4.18 and compiled with all PPP
modules (especially PPP ATM module)  in kernel.
2.Go the the olitec driver directory. Then compiled the e2.o (olitec
driver for conexant PPPoATM driver).
3.command: # insmod e2.o
4.command:  # ifconfig hsb0 up
5.command: ./dhcpcd hsb0
Now you should be able to see hsb0 device with IP Address of 10.0.0.3.
6.command: ping 10.0.0.2
ping should be successful
7. Go to http://10.0.0.2 from any browser.
8. Here you will be asked with userid and password. I entered as per
olitec documents and also tried userid/password given by Touchtel.   BUT
IT FAILS. :(  :(  Let us wait and  see..... :)  :)

Now I am working on it. Can anybody help me in this regard? anybody has
any suggestion?

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy

Hi,

Better give all solution on the basis of concepts and command line tool 
(No distribution specific or desktop specific GUI tool). There are two 
possibilities for this approach:

1 If the Interviewer is good in concepts and command line, you will be 
well judged by default.
2. If the Interviewer is not so good in these, he can't understand 
whether your answer is right or not. :)  :)

Both are advantageous to you! All the best,

Regards,
T.KaruppuSwamy

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Thu Oct 14 15:52:06 2004
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Thu Oct 14 15:42:21 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Sshd - unusual mode
In-Reply-To: <20041014050411.11B181DB274@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <20041014102206.GC12520@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

S Mohan wrote:
> I've done this. I could also set password auth off in sshd_config and
> install keys. As I had indicated earlier, I do not have control on machines
> that log in. Thus I need to work on a server-side only solution. I've
> specified the program in /etc/passwd, know it is secure and that the user
> cannot get a shell. The application users are not system users. Thus, I do
> not want to use any system auth mechanism at all.

1. What I have suggested IS a server side only solution.  There is no client
   config necessary at all - users will need to login using the "foo"
   username and without prompting for a password, your app will start.

   Set "foo" to something more meaningful like the name of your app.

2. You only need to create a *single* account for the application and all
   users will use the same.

- Raja

Hi ignacius,

We have good progress about it. I am confident that soon we will have
solution (if anybody is successful with this modem type, as i have
mentioned below, it is nice to inform through this mailing list). Here
is the history.

I too have touchtel 64kbps ADSL modem. I have started installing it on
Debian 3.0.r2.
My modem is Conexant ADSL Modem of vendor id: 0x0572 and product id:
0xcb06 (You have to check yours from any Windows installation done by
Touchtel). I have two options of driver.
1. accessrunner driver
2. olitec Aethra StarModem driver

Now I am working on olitec driver.:
1.I have installed kernel source 2.4.18 and compiled with all PPP
modules (especially PPP ATM module)  in kernel.
2.Go the the olitec driver directory. Then compiled the e2.o (olitec
driver for conexant PPPoATM driver).
3.command: # insmod e2.o
4.command:  # ifconfig hsb0 up
5.command: ./dhcpcd hsb0
Now you should be able to see hsb0 device with IP Address of 10.0.0.3.
6.command: ping 10.0.0.2
ping should be successful
7. Go to http://10.0.0.2 from any browser.
8. Here you will be asked with userid and password. I entered as per
olitec documents and also tried userid/password given by Touchtel.   
BUT
IT FAILS. :(  :(  Let us wait and  see..... :)  :)

Now I am working on it. Can anybody help me in this regard? anybody has
any suggestion?

Regards
T.KaruppuSwamy

Hi All,

I have successfully compiled Linux 2.6.7 on RedHat 9 and was really
happy to notice the increase in performance and responsiveness. X
Windows has become a lot more responsive.

However I am facing a peculiar problem. I have configured the system
for most IDE devices but yet my Samsung 40x CD-RW does not get
detected.

/dev/cdrom is not a valid block device. Any pointers.

Hardware as follows : Intel P4 1.7 GHz, Intel D845GLAD Motherboard,
128 MB DDR, Samsung 40 GB HDD,

In order to gain some more performance i had disabled the SCSI devices
as it was clearly mentioned that CD writing no longer needs SCSI
emulation. Also i was a bit skimpy while configuring USB devices as i
hardly ever use them .Hence the system does throw out some errors
while trying to load some USB drivers.

Also what i would like to know is what is the Cryprtographic API
support in the kernel for. Is it essential for generating random
numbers or using md5 and crypt kind of functions in languages like PHP
which provide inbuilt routines for these.

From swamytk at tandbintl.com  Fri Oct 15 18:17:34 2004
From: swamytk at tandbintl.com (T.KaruppuSwamy (T & B))
Date: Fri Oct 15 18:10:33 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] 2.6 Kernel doubts
In-Reply-To: <5800e9980410150528b32fa7b@mail.gmail.com>
References: <5800e9980410150528b32fa7b@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <416FC6E6.1080700@tandbintl.com>

Hi Batfan,

1. CD Writer issue: Try loading "ide-scsi" from command line and then 
try. It should work. For me it worked in 2.6.18 kernel
2. USB drivers failures: a new /sys file system has been introduced 
which will have all USB device related data. You can try changing the 
/proc occurrence in the /etc/rc.sysinit  script with the /sys for USB 
related lines.

All the best
T.KaruppuSwamy

      > first time and saw this.)

I have been using a very old Gimp 1.2 "pre-release", and now I notice,
version 2.0 supports scripting with perl, python and script-fu.  Surely,
the basic tools for drawing kolams are available in Gimp. But writing a
workable script may be needlessly complex for the simple task at hand.

Probably, XaoS could also be modified to generate kolams of astronomical
size.

Even DOM and Javascript, may provide a good interface for drawing kolams.

But I wonder if any serious research has been done into _how_ kolams are
drawn by hand.  I have had the pleasure of watching very complex kolams
getting drawn.  Many of the designs and patterns are traditionally
passed down, but I doubt if there is any authoritative treatise on the
subject, though it is one of the 64 arts [48:"art of framing mystical
diagrams"]. Documenting the basic syntax, grammar and rules of kolam
drawing along with its traditional terminology may prove useful.

Probably the first step is the draw the dot grid, for which it would be
worthwhile to create a standard notation. [XaoS could do without dot
grids] The next would be to start mapping a route - either using
formulas or by hand. The game is that dots are laid in a grid, and are 
"captured", and the final design has to be symmetrical to qualify as a 
kolam. The more complex the pattern, the more its "share value".

The closest thing I have done to a kolam program is the chess horse 
program at http://personal.vsnl.com/kr_chesshorse.html  It may give a 
few ideas on one approach for drawing kolams using a web interface.

Some Links that may be of use:

http://www.cmi.ac.in/gift/Kolam.htm
http://www.hindu.com/thehindu/mp/2003/01/07/stories/2003010700050200.htm
http://www.findarticles.com/p/articles/mi_hb010/is_200201/ai_hibm1G181528419
http://www.uni-koeln.de/phil-fak/indologie/kolam/preamble.html
http://www.uni-koeln.de/phil-fak/indologie/kolam/kolam1/kolamsmg.html
http://www.geocities.com/Athens/5180/kolam.html
http://www.americanscientist.org/template/AssetDetail/assetid/14424
http://www.ignca.nic.in/nl002608.htm
http://astronomy.swin.edu.au/~pbourke/curves/snake_kolam/
http://astronomy.swin.edu.au/~pbourke/curves/
http://astronomy.swin.edu.au/~pbourke/curves/maclaurintrisectrix/
http://astronomy.swin.edu.au/~pbourke/geomformats/
http://astronomy.swin.edu.au/~pbourke/fractals/interface/index.html
http://astronomy.swin.edu.au/~pbourke/geometry/
http://astronomy.swin.edu.au/~pbourke/geometry/

Regards,
Ramanraj.

Hi,

If you asked around for a distro for a particular purpose, you'll get
many different answers based on the experience of the people to whom you
are asking! Considering security top priority, I suggest you try either
Debian or Gentoo. Gentoo works on a similar package management system as
Debian but its source based. You also do not have to fall into
dependency hell, as the "emerge" package management system does all the
dependency resolution and installs all the necessary software. Regular
security updates are available as well.
Installing Qmail On Gentoo can be a breeze. Gentoo System are stable as
too(read 24/7).
Debian is know for its rock solid characteristics. Here too security is
given top priority and you can update security patches once in a while
and be safe.....

 
---
Regards,
Shuveb Hussain 
Visit my Blog www.livejournal.com/users/shuveb

I know this is not an exact solution, but Lomboz didn't work for me
either on Eclipse. Did you also install EMF(http://www.eclipse.org/emf/)
? It should be installed before you install Lomboz. It still didn't work
for me and I couldn't figure out why. Unless you *have* to work with
Eclipse, may I suggest jEdit (http://jedit.sourceforge.net). It's a lot
leaner than Eclipse, syntax-highlighting of JSP is done by default and
and there are a lot of plugins, you won't miss any functionality.

But if you *can* afford big money you can always go for IntellijIDEA
from JetBrains (http://www.intellij.com) which is somehow, acknowledged
as the best Java IDE around, hands down. But I'm happy with jEdit, it
works for me (I've given up trying to convince Emacs to become de-facto
Java IDE for me. Now don't show me JDEE. Been there, done that). 

-Vamsee Kanakala.

Writing a good GUI layer over Emacs (gtk2 is in gnu emacs cvs) with
excellent UI is what is needed now.  Emacs is extensible with Lisp and

gain some special programming skills that is worth even if he is not
going to program ever in Lisp.  And it will help me to use (my next
favorite) Emacs editor effectively.  The day when I would switch to
Emacs from Vi is not so far.

Subject: [Ilugc] Re: [OT] Regarding the Eclipse - weird gmail warning
In-Reply-To: <16754.7155.13138.117241@monster.linux.in>
References: <dc538c3f04101503383922fe55@mail.gmail.com>
	<3779a1e70410151831796a376d@mail.gmail.com>
	<dc538c3f041016011642bfe37d@mail.gmail.com>
	<8816fcf804101608314798f37c@mail.gmail.com>
	<16754.7155.13138.117241@monster.linux.in>
Message-ID: <32b5ee7604101710493616f3a6@mail.gmail.com>

Spam comes in a variety of forms, including fraudulent messages. This
mass-messaging is called 'spoofing' or 'password phishing.'

Such practices involve sending messages that appear to be from a
legitimate source and/or creating an official-looking webpage that
asks you to provide your username and password, or other personal
information including your Social Security number, bank account
number, PIN number, credit card number, mother's maiden name, or
birthday.

Spammers often ask for this information in an attempt to steal your
Gmail account, your money, your credit, and/or your identity.

Google is currently testing a service designed to alert Gmail users to
messages that appear to be phishing attacks. When the Gmail team
becomes aware of such an attack, the details of these messages are
used to automatically identify future suspected phishing attacks.

The result: when a Gmail user opens a suspected phishing message,
Gmail displays a warning.

Gmail's phishing alerts operate automatically, much like spam
filtering. Gmail's spam filters automatically divert messages that are
suspected of being unwanted messages into 'Spam'. Similarly, Gmail's
phishing alerts automatically display warnings with messages that are
suspected of being phishing attacks so that users know to take care
before providing any personal information.

You should always be wary of any message that asks for your personal
information, or messages that refer you to a webpage asking for
personal information. If you receive similar messages, especially from
a source claiming to be Google or Gmail, please do not provide the
information requested.

Here's what you can do to protect yourself and stop fraudsters:

    * Make sure the URL domain is correct, and click on any images and
links to verify that you are directed to proper pages within the site.
For example, the Gmail URL is http://gmail.google.com/ or, for even
more security, https://gmail.google.com/. Although some links may
appear to contain 'gmail.com,' you may be redirected to another site
after entering such addresses into your browser.
    * Always look for the closed lock icon in the status bar at the
bottom of your browser window whenever you enter any private
information, including your password.
    * Check the message headers. The 'From' field is easily
manipulated. There are several online tools which will help you verify
the source of a message. To view the header from a message in Gmail,
open the message, click 'More options,' and then click 'Show
original.' Copy everything from 'Delivered-To:' through the
'References:' line. To get headers from other webmail or email
providers, please refer to this page:
http://www.spamcop.com/help_with_headers/.
    * If you're still uncertain, contact the organization from which
the message appears to be sent. Don't use the reply address in the
message, since it can be forged. Instead, visit the official website
of the company in question, and find a different contact address.
    * If you enter your account or personal information as a result of
a spoof or phishing message, take action quickly. Send a copy of the
message header and the entire text of the message to the Federal Trade
Commission at uce@ftc.gov. If you entered credit card or bank account
numbers, contact your financial institution. If you think you may be
the victim of identity theft, contact your local police.
    * Gmail doesn't send unsolicited mass messages asking for
passwords or personal information. If you think your Gmail account has
been compromised, contact us at gmail-abuse@google.com. Please include
the header of the suspicious message and the entire message text.

this is the warning that i got for  balachander muruganandam's
link.Learn more- yielded the above.
Warning:  This message may not be from whom it claims to be. Beware of
following any links in it or of providing the sender with any personal
information.   Learn more

one is not that good (compare the GUI of IntelliJ and Emacs [1] )

[1] Projects 'cedet' are nothing but ugly hack when it comes to
rendering (they should use API like gtk+ for GUI, not some ugly X11
draw hack)

emacs is not really for a newbie, you know... It might seem a little
snobbish (or a lot, for that matter), but it's really meant for those
people who are already comfortable with the keyboard, or who want to
learn to use it effectively. A do-it-all GUI would really defeat the
whole purpose of emacs. Besides, it might just prove too complex to
integrate it into all that lisp code...

Shash

Everything is good about Emacs, but the point is it doesn't support
anti-aliased fonts or even have a good set of fonts.  This might be 
because it runs on many operating systems that don't have support for
anti-aliased fonts, etc.

But, Emacs can probably detect the OS and the font support and make use
of it.  Probably like Mozilla/Firefox.

From mksarav at gmail.com  Mon Oct 18 09:07:24 2004
From: mksarav at gmail.com (Saravanan M K)
Date: Mon Oct 18 21:37:31 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Book Review: CODE Reading -- The Open Source Perspective
In-Reply-To: <e2f046c0410180851425145de@mail.gmail.com>
References: <e2f046c04101808462c96432b@mail.gmail.com>
	<e2f046c0410180851425145de@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <e2f046c041018090769e98f51@mail.gmail.com>

Book Review: CODE Reading -- The Open Source Perspective

As a software developer most of the time, we spend adding new features
or functionalities in the existing code, written by somebody else. I
realized this after I joined Industry. Till date I hardly written any
code from scratch completely after I entered corporate environment. In
schools, colleges and Universities, all they teach us is how to code
using programming languages like C, C++ etc. Nobody teach us how to
read other's code. Infact that is what more important in a practical
point of view.

The following book which I am reading right now for the last 2 days,
is exactly teaches us How to read other's code? I should say, all the
software developers must learn this art. So if you find the time, go
and get a copy of this book and read it by all means.

CODE Reading
The Open Source Perspective

by

Diomidis Spinellis

ISBN: 0-201-79940-5
Addison Wesley/Pearson Education, 2003.

The author uses numerous real world examples to show us how to
identify good & bad code: how to read it, what to look for, and how to
use this knowledge to improve our own code.

Judgement: It is worth spending time to read this book in its
entirety.  You will write better code if you make it a habit to read
good code.

-- mks --

http://www.mksarav.org/blog/blog.html

My modem is marked as tera-100U terragate inc.

I installed the eciadsl usermode driver.

rpm -i eciadsl-usermode-0.9-2.i386.rpm

I got some kernel errors.So i upgrade the kernel t0 2.6.6.

After upgrading to kernel 2.6.6 for fedora core2 



My /etc/eciadsl/eciadsl.conf file

VID1=0915

PID1=8000

VID2=0915

PID2=8000

MODE=VCM_RFC2364

VCI=32

VPI=1

FIRMWARE=/etc/eciadsl/firmware00.bin

SYNCH=/etc/eciadsl/synch02.bin

PPPD_USER=myid_tn@touchtelindia.net

PPPD_PASSWD=imypassword

USE_DHCP=yes

USE_STATICIP=no

STATICIP=

GATEWAY=

MODEM=Other

PROVIDER=Other

DNS1=

DNS2=

My /etc/ppp/peers/adsl file 

# this file has been generated by the configuration tool of the ECIADSL driver

debug

kdebug 1

noipdefault

defaultroute

pty "/usr/local/bin/pppoeci -alt 4 -vpi 1 -vci 32 -vendor 0x0915 -product 0x8000 -mode VCM_RFC2364"

sync

user "myid_tn@touchtelindia.net"

noaccomp

nopcomp

noccp

novj

holdoff 10

# This will store the pid of pppd in the first line of /var/run/ppp-eciadsl.pid

# and the interface created (like ppp0) on the second line.

linkname eciadsl

# maxfail is the number of times pppd retries to execute pppoeci after

# an error. If you put 0, pppd retries forever, filling up the process table

# and thus, making the computer unusable.

maxfail 10

usepeerdns

noauth

# If your PPP peer answer to LCP EchoReq (lcp-echo requests), you can

# use the lcp-echo-failure to detect disconnected links with:

#

# lcp-echo-interval 600

# lcp-echo-failure 10

#

# However, if your PPP peer DOES NOT answer to lcp-echo request, you MUST

# desactivate this feature with the following line

#

lcp-echo-interval 0

# You may need the following, but ONLY as a workaround

# mtu 1432

persist

From ramanraj at md4.vsnl.net.in  Mon Oct 18 23:53:20 2004
From: ramanraj at md4.vsnl.net.in (Ramanraj K)
Date: Mon Oct 18 23:44:07 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Partial post or get
References: <20041018170700.5B0C71DB259@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <41740A18.2070009@md4.vsnl.net.in>

Sriram Krishnan wrote:
> What do you mean by partial post? If you want to send only some of the form
> values, you could do that by constructing your own query string for 'get'.
> This is of course if your server script is equipped to deal with such
> things. I'm curious though - why do you want to do this?

To get an idea about partial get, visit:
http://www.w3.org/Protocols/rfc2616/rfc2616-sec9.html
http://www.w3.org/Protocols/rfc2616/rfc2616-sec14.html

Partial post or get would help the same way a patch helps.

There is nothing novel about this.

A tcl/tk script could do this:

set so[socket quote.yahoo.com 80]
set q "/d/quotes.csv?s=MSFT&f=sl1dlt1c1ohgv"
puts $so "GET $q HTTP/1.0\n\n"
flush $so
puts [read $so]

If JavaScript could do the same, it could be made to do only a partial 
get or post (so far the user is concerned), though for the server 
script, it would be a regular get or post.

PS: save the tcl script as getMSquotes.tcl or something, and it could 
give an update about the stock prices of MS  whenever run.

My /etc/eciadsl/eciadsl.conf file
VID1=0915
PID1=8000
VID2=0915
PID2=8000
MODE=VCM_RFC2364
VCI=32
VPI=1
FIRMWARE=/etc/eciadsl/firmware00.bin

USE_DHCP=yes
USE_STATICIP=no
STATICIP=
GATEWAY=
MODEM=Other
PROVIDER=Other
DNS1=
DNS2=

My /etc/ppp/peers/adsl file 
# this file has been generated by the configuration
tool of the ECIADSL driver

debug
kdebug 1
noipdefault
defaultroute
pty "/usr/local/bin/pppoeci -alt 4 -vpi 1 -vci 32
-vendor 0x0915 -product 0x8000 -mode VCM_RFC2364"
sync
user "myid_tn@touchtelindia.net"
noaccomp
nopcomp
noccp
novj
holdoff 10
# This will store the pid of pppd in the first line of
/var/run/ppp-eciadsl.pid
# and the interface created (like ppp0) on the second
line.
linkname eciadsl
# maxfail is the number of times pppd retries to
execute pppoeci after
# an error. If you put 0, pppd retries forever,
filling up the process table
# and thus, making the computer unusable.
maxfail 10
usepeerdns
noauth
# If your PPP peer answer to LCP EchoReq (lcp-echo
requests), you can
# use the lcp-echo-failure to detect disconnected
links with:
#
# lcp-echo-interval 600
# lcp-echo-failure 10
#
# However, if your PPP peer DOES NOT answer to
lcp-echo request, you MUST
# desactivate this feature with the following line
#
lcp-echo-interval 0
# You may need the following, but ONLY as a workaround
# mtu 1432
persist

Oct 18 22:14:07 localhost pppd[3272]: secondary DNS
address 202.56.250.5

	
stopping the connection:
----------------------------
Just kill the pppd daemon:
Asroot:
# killall pppd

start the connection again?
-----------------------------
Re-start the pppd daemon this way:
As root:
# pppd call adsl
OR
As root:
#startmodem

especially for his help...

Are you  talking about  automated form submitting  methods or  are you

One thing to note is that lots of people write crappy code like:

if (!$variable1 && !$variable2 && ... !$variableN) { 
   # dont submit
}

so even  if you got  to partially submitting  a form, it might  not go
through because the code on the other end wont let you to!

traceroute -n 203.145.184.13

Or is it that though the link goes up, no packets go out through your 
gateway?

  Easy enough - just set up your /etc/resolv.conf with the
IP addresses of the nameservers (primary, secondary) provided
by Touchtel (this will allow DNS name resolution for hosts
that are not in your /etc/hosts).

Sivasankar Chander wrote:
>   The script seemed to update /etc/ppp/resolv.conf, not /etc/resolv.conf.
> I'm not sure of the implications, but maybe all he has to do is to
> copy the entries from the former into the latter.

/etc/ppp/options had "usepeerdns" in it.

That will basically auto-update resolv.conf with the appropriate values 
of dns received from the dhcp server at touchtel's end.

 >>of IntelliJ and Emacs [1] )
 >
 >
 > I really don't agree - the productivity gains of Emacs comes from the
 > keyboard. If you're using the mouse, you're better off using
